24:671:60097:44:25:72:309:615:144:Times:117:Times:V.  Consequences for Labor Force Participation 
24:672:60143:25:26:90:534:590:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:We now consider impacts of the Agent Orange policy on veterans’ employment and earnings. Using 
24:673:60238:26:25:72:526:564:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:models analogous (1) and (2), we test whether the fraction of BOG veterans in the labor force declined 
24:674:60339:25:25:72:523:539:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:differentially relative to NOG veterans following the 2001 policy change. We again include data from 
24:675:60439:25:32:72:470:514:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:1996, 1997, and 2007 because of the longer sample window available for SSA outcomes.  
24:676:60523:32:25:72:253:482:117:Times:117:Times:A.  Impacts on labor force participation 
24:677:60563:25:25:90:541:457:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Table 8 considers the impact of the Agent Orange policy on labor force participation, measured as the 
24:678:60665:25:25:72:538:432:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:percentage of living veterans in an SSA reporting cell who have positive labor earnings. The first column 
24:679:60770:25:25:72:531:407:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:finds that labor force participation among BOG veterans in the baseline year of 1996 was slightly lower 
24:680:60871:25:26:72:527:382:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:(by 0.32 points) among BOG than NOG veterans. This participation gap was modestly expanding (i.e., 
24:681:60965:26:25:72:512:356:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:becoming more negative) in the early part of our sample period, falling by an additional 0.81 points 
24:682:61065:25:25:72:518:331:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:between 1996 and 2001. This expansion accelerated after 2000, with the BOG relative to NOG labor 
24:683:61162:25:26:72:541:306:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:force participation rate falling by an additional 2.02 percentage points between 2001 and 2007. Column 2, 
24:684:61266:26:25:72:539:280:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:which fits the parameterized model in equation (2), shows the rate of divergence between BOG and NOG 
24:685:61364:25:25:72:530:255:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans roughly doubled after the Agent Orange decision, from 0.15 percentage points per year to 0.33 
24:686:61464:25:26:72:306:230:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:percentage points (0.15 + 0.18) annually after 2001.  
24:687:61514:26:25:90:512:204:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Coupled with the evidence in Table 5 on DC enrollments, the results in Table 8 suggest that the 
24:688:61607:25:25:72:533:179:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:differential increase in DC enrollment among BOG veterans spurred a reduction in their labor supply. A 
24:689:61708:25:25:72:499:154:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:natural alternative interpretation, however, is that BOG veterans were in worse health than NOG 
24:690:61802:25:26:72:510:129:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans—perhaps due to the rigors of in-theatre military service—leading to comparatively earlier 
24:691:61901:26:25:72:537:103:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:retirements in the 2000s for reasons unrelated to the 2001 policy change. If so, the accelerating decline in 
24:692:62008:25:0:72:536:78:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:LFP among BOG veterans after 2001 should primarily impact the oldest Vietnam veterans, with younger 
25:693:62110:0:25:72:504:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veteran cohorts exhibiting a similar LFP falloff as they approached these early retirement years in 
25:694:62208:25:25:72:534:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:subsequent years. Figure 7 and the remaining two panels of Table 8 explore these competing hypotheses 
25:695:62308:25:25:72:535:659:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:by again subdividing the sample into two birth cohorts of average ages 54 and 51 years at the time of the 
25:696:62410:25:26:72:536:634:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:policy change. Both the figure and the table reveal that labor force participation of BOG relative to NOG 
25:697:62516:26:25:72:530:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans for both sets of birth cohorts dropped sharply soon after the policy change. The year-over-year 
25:698:62620:25:25:72:536:583:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:decline in BOG LFP relative to NOG LFP doubled after 2001 for both older (born 1946-48) and younger 
25:699:62719:25:26:72:519:558:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:(born 1949-1951) cohorts, rising from 0.17 to 0.36 percentage points (0.17 + 0.19) among the former 
25:700:62814:26:25:72:532:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:group, and from 0.14 to 0.32 percentage points (0.14 + 0.18) among the latter group. This trend break in 
25:701:62915:25:25:72:531:507:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:BOG relative to NOG labor force participation occurring simultaneously across birth cohorts after 2001 
25:702:63015:25:26:72:537:482:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:suggests that benefits expansion rather than early retirements explains the sharp drop in BOG labor force 
25:703:63121:26:25:72:301:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:participation following the Agent Orange decision.  
25:704:63172:25:25:90:504:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:The upper panel of Table 9 explores these employment patterns by race and AFQT subgroup. 
25:705:63260:25:25:72:532:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Declines in LFP generally mirror uptake of DC across demographic groups. Consistent with the Table 6 
25:706:63361:25:26:72:531:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:findings for DC enrollment, the fall in labor force participation among nonwhite and among low-AFQT 
25:707:63461:26:25:72:533:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:BOG relative to NOG veterans following the 2001 policy change is more pronounced than among white 
25:708:63557:25:32:72:529:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and higher-AFQT veterans. These differences across groups are not statistically significant, however.    
25:709:63660:32:24:72:242:298:117:Times:117:Times:B.  Impacts on labor market earnings 
25:710:63696:24:26:90:538:274:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Alongside its extensive margin impact, receipt of DC benefits may spur veterans to reduce their work 
25:711:63795:26:25:72:506:248:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:hours or switch from full to part-time employment, thus reducing earnings conditional on ongoing 
25:712:63891:25:25:72:542:223:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:employment. We explore the effect of the Agent Orange policy on total labor force earnings by estimating 
25:713:63993:25:25:72:514:198:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:equation (2) for the log of mean cell earnings, excluding (of necessity) cells where all veterans have 
25:714:64094:25:47:72:513:173:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:exited the labor force.39 Panel B of Table 9 shows that earnings averaged about 2.6 log points lower 
25:715:64189:47:13:216:219:126:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:                                                        
25:716:64244:13:16:72:530:113:42:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:39 We use the log of the mean rather than the mean of the log because of the cell-level aggregation of our earnings 
25:717:64359:16:12:72:539:97:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:data. We do not, however, adjust cell means for non-participation; if a cell contains five veterans each earning $25K 
25:718:64477:12:11:72:537:85:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:annually and one leaves the labor force, mean cell earnings falls to $20K. Thus, this measure incorporates intensive 
25:719:64594:11:0:72:217:74:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:and extensive margin adjustments.   
26:720:64631:0:25:72:538:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:among BOG than NOG veterans in our baseline year, and this gap was expanding by about 0.2 log points 
26:721:64730:25:25:72:507:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:per year through 2001. The earnings gap grew significantly more rapidly—by about 0.7 log points 
26:722:64822:25:25:72:542:659:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:annually (0.23 + 0.45)—following the 2001 policy change. Once again, the effects are larger for nonwhite 
26:723:64925:25:26:72:187:634:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and low-AFQT veterans.  
26:724:64948:26:25:90:521:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Since these total earnings impacts combine extensive margin (participation) and intensive margin 
26:725:65045:25:25:72:519:583:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:(hours and wage) responses, we cannot directly infer whether they reflect changes in earnings among 
26:726:65143:25:26:72:538:558:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:incumbents or merely a reduction in the number of veterans working. The evidence in panel A of Table 9 
26:727:65245:26:25:72:530:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:suggests, however, that minority and low-AFQT veterans were particularly likely to exit the labor force 
26:728:65349:25:25:72:538:507:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:upon receiving DC benefits. If we hypothesize more generally that veterans with lower potential earnings 
26:729:65454:25:26:72:538:482:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:are most likely to exit the labor force in response to increased transfer income, we can compare extensive 
26:730:65560:26:25:72:508:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:margin and total earnings responses to assess evidence for intensive margin responses. Concretely, 
26:731:65659:25:25:72:521:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:suppose that earnings among those dropping out of the labor force are below the average of those still 
26:732:65762:25:25:72:516:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:working within the cell—that is, income effects are larger for low earnings workers. In this case, the 
26:733:65864:25:26:72:492:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:decline in log cell earnings will be smaller than the decline in log cell labor force participation. 
26:734:65964:26:25:72:531:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Conversely, if the decline in log cell earnings exceeds the decline in log cell participation, this indicates 
26:735:66074:25:25:72:532:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:that either earnings is also falling on the intensive margin or, contrary to our assumption, higher earning 
26:736:66182:25:26:72:306:305:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:workers are exiting employment disproportionately.  
26:737:66233:26:25:90:531:279:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:To facilitate earnings and employment comparisons, panel C of Table 9 reports estimates where the 
26:738:66330:25:25:72:497:254:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:dependent variable is the log of the fraction of veterans in a cell working (rather than simply the 
26:739:66429:25:25:72:534:229:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:percentage working, as in panel A). Comparing across panels B and C reveals that the decline in relative 
26:740:66532:25:26:72:509:204:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:earnings of BOG versus NOG veterans after 2001 is, in most cases, slightly larger than the relative 
26:741:66631:26:25:72:539:178:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:decline in labor force participation. In column 1, for example, the relative decline in log earnings of BOG 
26:742:66739:25:25:72:528:153:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:relative to NOG veterans expands by 0.45 log points per year after 2001 whereas the relative decline in 
26:743:66842:25:26:72:529:128:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:log LFP increases by only 0.36 log points per year. This pattern also holds for black and white veterans 
26:744:66946:26:25:72:520:102:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:considered separately, though it does not hold for lower and higher-AFQT veterans. We infer that the 
26:745:67045:25:0:72:498:77:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Agent Orange policy likely induced a mixture of labor force exit and earnings reductions among 
27:746:67140:0:25:72:412:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:beneficiaries, though the evidence on the latter margin is far from clear cut.   
27:747:67220:25:31:72:75:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
27:748:67220:31:25:72:504:653:144:Times:117:Times:VI.  Comparing Labor Supply and Enrollment Impacts: Instrumental Variables Estimates 
27:749:67304:25:26:90:516:628:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Motivated by the evidence that the Agent Orange policy both raised DC enrollment and lowered 
27:750:67391:26:25:72:525:602:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:earnings among eligible veterans, we now use the Agent Orange policy as an instrumental variable for 
27:751:67491:25:25:72:539:577:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:receipt of DC benefits. This instrumental variables approach provides a valid estimate of the causal effect 
27:752:67596:25:26:72:492:552:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:of DC benefits on labor supply under the assumption that the Agent Orange policy only affects 
27:753:67688:26:25:72:542:526:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:employment and earnings through its impact on benefits enrollment and transfer payments. This exclusion 
27:754:67792:25:25:72:525:501:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:restriction is untestable of course, but the panoply of findings above confer credibility: we find a sharp 
27:755:67896:25:26:72:513:476:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:rise in DC receipt, DC payments, and total disability income among BOG relative to NOG veterans 
27:756:67992:26:25:72:520:450:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:following adoption of the Agent Orange policy; the rise in take-up was equally steep and pronounced 
27:757:68091:25:25:72:538:425:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:among younger and older veterans, and was greatest among nonwhite and low-AFQT veterans; and in all 
27:758:68190:25:25:72:511:400:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:cases, take-up responses are paralleled by differential employment and earnings drops among BOG 
27:759:68286:25:26:72:537:375:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:relative to NOG veterans that occur among both older and younger veterans, and which are slightly more 
27:760:68389:26:25:72:299:349:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:pronounced among nonwhite and low-AFQT vets.  
27:761:68434:25:25:90:530:324:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Table 10 presents instrumental variables of equation (2) for the impact of DC participation on labor 
27:762:68535:25:26:72:539:299:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:force participation, where the endogenous variable in panel A is the percentage of a cell enrolled in DC.40 
27:763:68642:26:25:72:534:273:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:The 2SLS estimate in column (1) finds that each percentage point increase in DC enrollment reduces the 
27:764:68745:25:25:72:530:248:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:fraction of veterans working by 0.18 points—that is, approximately one veteran exits the labor force for 
27:765:68849:25:25:72:521:223:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:every five veterans newly awarded DC benefits. Comparing across rows of this table, we find slightly 
27:766:68950:25:26:72:500:198:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:larger employment effects for nonwhite and low-AFQT veterans, consistent with our maintained 
27:767:69043:26:25:72:505:172:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:hypothesis that participation among these groups is more elastic. Notably, the (scaled) labor force 
27:768:69143:25:31:72:522:147:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:participation impact is estimated to be slightly (though not significantly) larger for younger than older 
27:769:69248:31:13:216:219:116:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:                                                        
27:770:69303:13:16:72:533:103:42:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:40 We limit the sample to the years 1998 through 2006 for which DC measures are available, rather than the longer 
27:771:69416:16:12:72:536:87:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:sample window of 1996 through 2007 for which SSA earnings data are available. The instrumental variable for DC 
27:772:69527:12:0:72:266:75:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:enrollment is 퐵푂퐺"×푡−2001×1푡≥2002. 
28:773:69563:0:25:72:541:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans, again underscoring that the results are unlikely to be simply driven by differential trends in early 
28:774:69673:25:25:72:297:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:retirement among BOG relative to NOG veterans.  
28:775:69719:25:25:90:539:659:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:By specifying DC participation as the endogenous variable, the panel A estimate does not account for 
28:776:69818:25:26:72:535:634:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:policy-induced increases in DC benefits along the intensive margin—higher benefits among incumbents, 
28:777:69919:26:25:72:525:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and greater potential benefits among new enrollees. We relax this restriction in panel B by making our 
28:778:70022:25:25:72:525:583:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:endogenous variable the sum of disability income (DC, SSDI and SSI benefits). This variable captures 
28:779:70123:25:26:72:523:558:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:changes in transfer payments among both new enrollees and incumbents.41 The panel B estimates find 
28:780:70221:26:25:72:534:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:that each thousand dollars in disability benefits payment reduces the probability of a veteran working by 
28:781:70326:25:25:72:540:507:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:approximately 0.80 percentage points, with slightly larger impacts among nonwhite veterans (0.97 points) 
28:782:70429:25:26:72:538:482:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and slightly smaller impacts among older veterans (0.70 points). Scaling these estimates by the mean rate 
28:783:70532:26:25:72:516:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:of labor force participation (84.7 points) and mean year 2000 earnings (in constant $2013 dollars) of 
28:784:70633:25:25:72:537:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:$52.5K (Appendix Table 4) implies an extensive margin labor force participation elasticity of -0.50. This 
28:785:70737:25:25:72:535:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:is similar in magnitude to the estimates reported by Boyle and Lahey (2010), who study the labor supply 
28:786:70839:25:26:72:536:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:of a relatively comparable set of veterans who were nearing retirement in the mid-1990s. We also cannot 
28:787:70943:26:25:72:529:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:rule out that the participation elasticity we obtain incorporates both pure (non-incentive) income effects 
28:788:71050:25:25:72:532:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:from increased transfer income and additional incentive effects stemming from the potential availability 
28:789:71155:25:26:72:522:305:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:of IU and SSDI benefits. Fully distinguishing these incentive and non-incentive effects remains a ripe 
28:790:71256:26:25:72:172:279:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:topic for future work.  
28:791:71279:25:25:90:533:254:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:To what degree is this causal effect driven by changes in labor force participation among incumbent 
28:792:71378:25:25:72:531:229:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:DC recipients—many of whom received a higher combined disability ratings and corresponding benefit 
28:793:71477:25:26:72:528:204:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:increases as a consequence of the Agent Orange policy—rather than by changes in participation among 
28:794:71577:26:25:72:512:178:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:new enrollees? Appendix Table 5 probes this question by comparing the evolution of CDRs among 
28:795:71671:25:50:72:523:153:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans according to DC enrollment status as of 1998 (the earliest year for which we have enrollment

30:833:75328:45:25:72:225:589:144:Times:117:Times:VII.  Impacts on Total Earnings 
30:834:75359:25:25:90:526:564:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Since the Agent Orange policy precipitated a rise in transfer payments and fall in employment and 
30:835:75457:25:25:72:498:539:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:earnings among eligible veterans, its net impact on incomes of BOG relative to NOG veterans is 
30:836:75552:25:26:72:526:514:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:ambiguous. We compare trends in total measured income (earnings plus the sum of DC, SSDI and SSI 
30:837:75648:26:25:72:526:488:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:benefits) between BOG and NOG veterans in Table 11, again limiting to the years 1998 through 2006, 
30:838:75747:25:25:72:510:463:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:where we have all earnings and benefits variables available. Since we have already established that 
30:839:75846:25:25:72:538:438:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:employment and earnings respond endogenously to policy-induced shifts in disability transfer income (as 
30:840:75950:25:26:72:537:413:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:theory would predict), the current exercise should be viewed as descriptive rather than inferential; the net 
30:841:76057:26:25:72:500:387:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:impact of the Agent Orange policy on veterans’ income combines exogenous policy impacts and 
30:842:76149:25:25:72:227:362:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:endogenous behavioral responses.  
30:843:76182:25:26:90:533:337:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:The first column of Table 11 (panel A) shows that, at the start of sample window in 1998, measured 
30:844:76280:26:25:72:530:311:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:incomes of BOG veterans were slightly lower than those of NOG veterans, with gaps of 0.75 log points 
30:845:76379:25:25:72:525:286:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:overall, 0.80 log points among nonwhites, and 0.70 log points among whites.44 Notably, incomes were 
30:846:76475:25:26:72:532:261:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:significantly higher (by 3.7 log points) among low-AFQT BOG veterans and significantly lower (by 2.5 
30:847:76575:26:25:72:538:235:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:log points) among high-AFQT BOG veterans (relative to their NOG counterparts). Recall, we saw earlier 
30:848:76677:25:25:72:539:210:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:in panel B of Table 9 that labor earnings of BOG veterans averaged up to 5 log points below that of NOG 
30:849:76779:25:25:72:522:185:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans. Thus, comparing Tables 9 and 11 reveals that disability transfer income largely made up the 
30:850:76880:25:26:72:531:160:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:difference between BOG and NOG veterans, and resulted in substantially higher income for low-AFQT 
30:851:76977:26:31:72:530:134:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:BOG veterans relative to low-AFQT NOG veterans, consistent with the findings of Angrist et al (2010) 
30:852:77076:31:13:216:219:103:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:                                                        
30:853:77131:13:16:72:520:90:42:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:44 These reported earnings are covariate adjusted since they derive from the Table 11 regression estimates. Raw 
30:854:77241:16:0:72:341:74:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:differences are similar, however, as may be inferred from Table 3.  
31:855:77310:0:25:72:198:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:for low-education veterans.  
31:856:77338:25:25:90:542:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:The second and third rows of Table 11 summarize the evolution of the BOG/NOG income differential 
31:857:77434:25:25:72:523:659:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:before and after the Agent Orange policy. Prior to the policy change, BOG veterans were on a slightly 
31:858:77534:25:26:72:517:634:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:more positive total income trend than NOG veterans, with average annual incomes in the full sample 
31:859:77633:26:25:72:502:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:rising by 0.20 log points annually in relative terms. This differential trend steepened significantly 
31:860:77733:25:25:72:535:583:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:following the policy change, jumping from 0.20 to 0.71 log points (0.20 + 0.51) annually. For nonwhites 
31:861:77837:25:26:72:521:558:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and low-AFQT veterans, the increase in the trajectory was steeper, rising from 0.27 to 1.31 log points 
31:862:77939:26:25:72:523:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:annually for the former group, and from 0.33 to 1.19 log points for the latter. While the Agent Orange 
31:863:78041:25:25:72:530:507:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:policy sharply reduced employment and earnings among eligible veterans, the Table 11 estimates make 
31:864:78141:25:26:72:493:482:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:clear that the policy-induced rise in transfer income more than offset these earnings reductions. 
31:865:78236:26:25:90:519:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:As a final characterization of these net policy and behavioral effects, the lower panel of Table 11 
31:866:78335:25:25:72:542:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:summarizes the net impact of DC enrollment on total earnings, where DC enrollment is instrumented with 
31:867:78438:25:25:72:524:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the Agent Orange policy. The outcome variable for these estimates is cell total income—earnings plus 
31:868:78538:25:26:72:532:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:disability benefits—and the endogenous variable is again DC enrollment. The point estimate of 0.52 for 
31:869:78641:26:25:72:529:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the full sample implies that - if a cell increased from 0 to 20 percent enrolled in DC - then average total 
31:870:78746:25:25:72:533:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veteran income in the cell would increase by about 10.4 percent. In interpreting this sizable impact, note 
31:871:78852:25:26:72:540:305:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:that we found above that only one in five (18 percent of) newly enrolled veterans exited the labor force as 
31:872:78960:26:25:72:541:279:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:a consequence of the Agent Orange policy. For the remaining four-fifths, enrollment in DC raised transfer 
31:873:79066:25:25:72:537:254:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:income while generating only minimal offsetting reductions in labor income, thus unambiguously raising 
31:874:79169:25:25:72:524:229:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:total income. Of course, average incomes of Vietnam era veterans were modest in the early 2000s and 
31:875:79268:25:26:72:527:204:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:remained modest net of transfer benefits following the Agent Orange policy change. Nevertheless, this 
31:876:79370:26:25:72:540:178:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:policy had the unusual effect of increasing average veteran incomes, inclusive of the foregone earnings of 
31:877:79476:25:44:72:476:153:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the approximately one in five newly enrolled DC recipients induced to exit the labor force.  
31:878:79565:44:25:72:153:109:144:Times:117:Times:VIII.  Discussion 
31:879:79582:25:0:90:526:84:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:This paper provides evidence that the policy-induced increase in enrollment in the VA’s Disability 
32:880:79681:0:25:72:538:709:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Compensation program had a significant effect on the labor supply of Vietnam-era veterans. We estimate 
32:881:79783:25:25:72:526:684:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:that 18 percent of individuals who became eligible for the DC program as a result of the policy change 
32:882:79885:25:25:72:494:659:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:dropped out of the labor force. Analyses that explore the effect on average earnings support the 
32:883:79982:25:26:72:515:634:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:conclusion that DC enrollment substantially lowered labor supply among Vietnam-era veterans who 
32:884:80078:26:25:72:530:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:served in the Vietnam theatre during the conflict there. These effects appear to be driven by those made 
32:885:80182:25:25:72:520:583:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:newly eligible for DC benefits rather than by increases in benefits among those already receiving DC 
32:886:80283:25:26:72:507:558:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:prior to the 2001 policy change. The increase in transfer income more than offsets the reduction in 
32:887:80383:26:25:72:526:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:earnings, so that average income among BOG veterans increased relative to their counterparts who did 
32:888:80483:25:25:72:537:507:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:not serve in theatre. Combining policy-induced increases in transfer income and reductions in labor force 
32:889:80588:25:26:72:536:482:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:participation, we estimate an extensive margin labor supply elasticities of -.50, which is somewhat larger 
32:890:80692:26:25:72:539:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:than consensus estimates, though not implausible for this near-elderly population of Vietnam era veterans 
32:891:80796:25:25:72:170:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:in diminished health.  
32:892:80818:25:25:90:542:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:It is also likely that the income effect of DC income on employment and earnings is augmented by the 
32:893:80918:25:26:72:538:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:interaction between DC enrollment and veterans’ potential eligibility for Individual Unemployability and 
32:894:81023:26:25:72:496:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:SSDI benefits, both of which provide strong incentives against gainful labor force participation. 
32:895:81121:25:25:72:535:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Consistent with this hypothesis, we find that the Agent Orange decision affected enrollment in two other 
32:896:81225:25:26:72:515:305:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:federal disability programs, raising enrollment in SSDI by approximately one recipient for every ten 
32:897:81325:26:25:72:540:279:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans newly enrolled in DC, and slightly reducing enrollment in the means-tested SSI program (though 
32:898:81427:25:25:72:541:254:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the estimated effects are an order of magnitude smaller than for SSDI). In addition, 14 percent of Vietnam 
32:899:81533:25:25:72:536:229:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:era veterans within our sample received IU status by 2006. Among veterans who enrolled in DC the year 
32:900:81635:25:26:72:539:204:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:after the Agent Orange policy change, fully one-third received IU status or a CDR of 100 by 2006 . Since 
32:901:81738:26:25:72:518:178:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:IU benefits are only available to veterans with earnings at or below the poverty threshold for a single 
32:902:81841:25:25:72:531:153:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:individual, the rapid growth of IU designations among newly enrolled DC beneficiaries underscores the 
32:903:81942:25:26:72:531:128:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:potential for the graduated DC benefit program to generate unintended labor supply impacts. Analyzing 
32:904:82042:26:25:72:533:102:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the dynamic interaction between these incentive and non-incentive effects of disability benefit programs 
32:905:82146:25:0:72:232:77:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:is a worthy goal for future research. 
33:906:82186:0:24:72:171:708:144:Times:117:Times:IX.  Data Appendix 
33:907:82204:24:13:72:327:684:117:Times:117:Times:A.   Construction of Cells in the BOG and NOG Samples 
33:908:82256:13:13:72:75:671:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:909:82256:13:12:72:514:658:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:To construct cells for matching individuals in the BOG and NOG samples with SSA data, we group 
33:910:82351:12:13:72:534:646:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:individuals based on their values of certain background characteristics, including their gender, race, year 
33:911:82459:13:13:72:528:633:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:of birth, and so forth. The list of variables used to form cells, ranked in the order in which the grouping 
33:912:82566:13:12:72:179:620:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:occurred, is as follows:  
33:913:82591:12:13:72:75:608:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:914:82591:13:13:90:219:595:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:1.  Gender (male or female) 
33:915:82618:13:12:90:223:582:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:2.  Race (white or nonwhite) 
33:916:82646:12:13:90:209:570:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:3.  Death year (e.g. 1985) 
33:917:82672:13:13:90:220:557:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:4.  Year-of-birth (e.g. 1946) 
33:918:82701:13:12:90:204:544:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:5.  Start year (e.g. 1966) 
33:919:82727:12:13:90:407:532:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:6.  Education at entry (e.g. 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 for hsd, hsg, smc, clg, clg-plus) 
33:920:82803:13:13:90:236:519:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:7.  AFQT score quintile (e.g. 2) 
33:921:82835:13:12:90:204:506:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:8.  Loss year (e.g. 1972) 
33:922:82860:12:13:90:270:494:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:9.  Region of residence (e.g. Northeast) 
33:923:82900:13:13:72:75:481:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:924:82900:13:12:72:75:468:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:925:82900:12:13:72:537:456:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Before forming cells, we determined which individuals could be verified upon matching to the SSA data. 
33:926:83003:13:12:72:526:443:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:A match would be verified if the social security number, date of birth, and at least six letters of the last 
33:927:83111:12:13:72:539:431:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:name could be matched in the two data sets. We construct cells from the verified BOG and NOG samples 
33:928:83211:13:13:72:529:418:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:so that there are between five and nine individuals in each cell. Each cell consists only of individuals in 
33:929:83315:13:12:72:525:405:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the BOG or in the NOG. The number of variables used in the grouping varies across cells. This occurs 
33:930:83416:12:13:72:535:393:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:because in some cases, a cell reaches a size of five to nine after grouping on a relatively small number of 
33:931:83522:13:13:72:534:380:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:variables. If a cell is between 10 and 29 individuals, we do not split further, but instead split the cell into 
33:932:83634:13:12:72:506:367:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the maximum number of cells with size five or more after sorting on the next matching variable to 
33:933:83731:12:13:72:534:355:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:maximize similarity within the cells. If a cell has fewer than five individuals then we re-merge it with an 
33:934:83838:13:13:72:534:342:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:adjacent cell. If a cell with fewer than five individuals is merged with an adjacent cell to form a new cell 
33:935:83946:13:12:72:356:329:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:with more than nine individuals, the merged cell is split in two.  
33:936:84011:12:13:72:75:317:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:937:84011:13:13:72:354:304:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:The distribution of the cell size for the verified NOG sample is: 
33:938:84076:13:13:72:75:291:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
33:939:84076:13:12:168:450:278:107:g_d0_f1:107:g_d0_f1:In Cell of Size Frequency Percentage 
33:940:84110:12:13:196:441:266:107:g_d0_f1:107:g_d0_f1:5 1,388,440 58.86

33:942:84142:12:13:196:445:241:107:g_d0_f1:107:g_d0_f1:7 171,269 7.26   
33:943:84159:13:12:196:445:228:107:g_d0_f1:107:g_d0_f1:8 70,048 2.97   
33:944:84175:12:13:196:445:216:107:g_d0_f1:107:g_d0_f1:9 71,271 3.02

34:974:84759:13:13:72:253:482:117:Times:117:Times:B.  Construction of the Analysis Sample 
34:975:84798:13:12:90:93:469:117:Times:117:Times: 
34:976:84798:12:13:72:525:457:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Appendix Figure 1A diagrams the construction of the sample used in our analysis. The “loss year” file 
34:977:84899:13:12:72:537:444:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and the Vietnam file combine to form our baseline OEMA sample of 4.1 million veterans. After merging 
34:978:85000:12:13:72:533:432:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:the OEMA sample to VA disability data, the SSA Death Master File, and SSA earnings information, we 
34:979:85099:13:13:72:513:419:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:restrict our sample to 3.8 million veterans who had valid SSA earnings data. As seen in Table 2, the 
34:980:85200:13:12:72:523:406:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:number of BOG veterans in our database is largest in the 1966 through 1971 start years; veterans who 
34:981:85301:12:13:72:540:394:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:began their service after 1971 tended not to serve in the Vietnam theatre while those entering before 1966 
34:982:85408:13:13:72:521:381:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:are much less likely to be included in our sample since many in the latter group left the Army prior to 
34:983:85512:13:12:72:511:368:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:1968, the first year of our “loss year” file. We therefore restrict both the BOG and NOG samples to 
34:984:85612:12:13:72:540:356:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans who have a start year between 1966 and 1971 inclusive, which reduces our sample to 1.9 million 
34:985:85714:13:13:72:524:343:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:veterans.45 We further restrict attention to individuals born between 1946 and 1951 inclusive, with 1.5 
34:986:85816:13:12:72:518:330:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:million veterans remaining. We next exclude approximately 150,000 veterans who have missing loss 
34:987:85913:12:13:72:534:318:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:years, loss years before 1968, or loss years after 1985. We finally drop an additional 8,000 veterans who 
34:988:86019:13:13:72:538:305:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:are in SSA cells where not all veterans have the same birth year, at least one veteran in the cell has a start 
34:989:86130:13:12:72:541:292:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:year before 1966 or after 1971, or at least one veteran in the cell has a loss year before 1968 or after 1985. 
34:990:86240:12:13:72:539:280:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:Our final sample includes 1.351 million veterans of the U.S. Army who began their service between 1966 
34:991:86342:13:13:72:531:267:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:and 1971 and were born between 1946 and 1951. For the analysis, we converted this final sample into a 
34:992:86444:13:12:72:496:254:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:1996-2007 panel of 15.2 million (year) x (individual) observations, or 2.9 million (year) x (cell) 
34:993:86543:12:13:72:299:242:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:observations, as depicted in Appendix Figure 1B.46 
34:994:86593:13:62:72:75:229:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1: 
34:995:86593:62:14:216:219:167:117:g_d0_f1:117:g_d0_f1:                                                        
34:996:86648:14:16:72:524:153:42:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:45 For the nearly 200,000 veterans with missing start years, we imputed their start year based on the median start 
34:997:86762:16:11:72:539:137:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:year for other veterans in the sample with the same date of birth. This has little bearing on our final sample as nearly 
34:998:86883:11:13:72:497:126:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:all veterans with missing start years have missing loss years and are therefore excluded from our analysis. 
34:999:86990:13:16:72:527:113:42:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:46 A veteran who dies in year t is dropped from the analysis sample in year t and in all subsequent years. Because 
34:1000:87102:16:12:72:525:97:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:year-of-death is one of the variables used when constructing cells, typically all members of a cell die in the same 
34:1001:87218:12:11:72:530:85:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:year (if any die). The number of surviving cells falls by approximately 4.8 percent from 1996 to 2007. We restrict 
34:1002:87333:11:0:72:488:74:97:g_d0_f1:97:g_d0_f1:our panel to 1998 through 2006 for all specifications where the outcome is based on VA disability data.
